The Gao Ming Association of Guangzhou, due to the sudden rise of the Xijiang River and the extremely tragic situation, urgently requested relief and telegraphed the Guang Zhao Association to request compassion and immediate relief to save the people affected by the disaster. Yesterday, the Guang Zhao Association and the Guangdong Overseas Chinese Business Federation jointly remitted 3,000 yuan to provide disaster relief.

Hubei Association Receives Telegram from Chamber of Commerce

The Shanghai Hubei Fellow Association yesterday received a telegram from the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Hubei Provincial Federation of Commerce, which read, "To all charitable organizations, we respectfully inform you that during this year's summer flood season, continuous rain has caused endless flooding. Recently, the Han River and the Yangtze River have risen simultaneously, and the embankments along the banks have been breached. In particular, Fancheng and Xiangyang in the upper reaches of the Han River have been completely submerged, with water reaching ten feet high, and the people have become fish. Han, Mian, Tian, and Qian have been submerged in a vast expanse of water. The rapid currents have swept away residents who could not escape in time, drowning hundreds of thousands of people. Corpses are floating everywhere, a sight that is unbearable to witness and a tragedy that is unbearable to hear. Wuhan is located at the confluence of the two rivers, and the situation is precarious. The existing embankments are all in danger of collapsing and are being reinforced day and night. Even if they can be preserved, it will only be a small area that is unharmed, while the disaster is even more severe than twenty years ago. Those affected by the disaster are struggling to provide relief and are in dire need of assistance. We earnestly ask that you consider the previous circumstances and show great compassion, either by allocating public funds to provide emergency relief or by donating from your private wealth to help the survivors. We appeal for benevolent governance and call out in unison. The telegram is urgent and expresses our deep concern. Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Hubei Provincial Federation of Commerce, together respectfully plead." Xiao.

Ministry of Communications to Reorganize Navigation Administration; Director Gao to Draft Plan

The New Voice News Agency reports that the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, in view of the decline of the shipping industry, resolved at a general meeting of members to request the government to allocate 10 million yuan in shipping industry bonds for relief. It also decided to implement self-restraint and to cooperate to prevent competition among companies. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, San Bei Steam Navigation Company, Ning Shao Steam Navigation Company, Butterfield & Swire, Jardine Matheson, Nisshin Kisen Kaisha, and six other companies have reached a concrete agreement on cooperation on the Yangtze River route, which will soon be implemented. The reorganization of other shipping routes is also in progress. The Ministry of Communications, in order to reorganize the national navigation administration, has instructed Gao Tingzi, Director of the Navigation Administration Department, to draft a reorganization plan. It has also instructed the Shipping Industry Association to maintain the status quo on all routes before the plan is promulgated. It has ordered the Maoli wheel of the Maoli Steamship Bureau and the Hongxing wheel of the Daxing Company to temporarily suspend operations. Requests to the Shanghai Navigation Bureau for permission to open new routes have reportedly been referred to the Ministry of Communications.

Shanghai-Ningbo Route: Recent Decline in Shipping Industry

Since the four companies operating on the Ningbo route began cooperating and sharing profits, business has improved considerably. In recent years, it has been difficult to make profits on various routes along the coast and the Yangtze River. However, the four companies operating on the Shanghai-Ningbo route, such as Xin Jiang Tian, Xin Ning Shao, Ning Xing, and Xin Beijing, have all had annual surpluses. Even the Xin Hong Xing wheel of the Daxing Company has been profitable. However, in the last month or two, the shipping industry on this route has also been affected by the sluggish market and the lack of purchasing power among the people. Exports have plummeted, and freight revenue has fallen sharply. The companies initially thought it was a fluke, but recently it has been happening on every voyage. The Ningbo wheels traveling from Shanghai to Ningbo are earning an average of 300 yuan for freight, and in some cases only 200 yuan, which is only one-tenth of the normal amount. Inbound freight to Shanghai, apart from a small amount of cotton, is also lacking. Import freight rates have also fallen drastically. According to people in the companies, the decline in business on the Shanghai-Ningbo route is unprecedented since the founding of the Republic. They also said that frequent natural disasters and rural bankruptcy mean there is little hope for recovery. This is a great misfortune for the shipping industry.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Newly Purchased Seagoing Vessel Named Haiyun (Sea Cloud), Operating to Lianyungang Because It Is a Seagoing Vessel

The state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company purchased the seagoing vessel Dafei from France. It was initially purchased under the name of Liu Hongsheng, so it was temporarily renamed Hongyuan. After arriving in Shanghai, it entered the Jiangnan Shipyard for inspection and repairs. The company has now completed the acceptance and decided to send it to Lianyungang (Old Wharf) to transport cargo for combined transport, in order to avoid renting ships from other companies and spending more than 100,000 yuan per year on rent, thus reducing unnecessary expenses. The chief captain of the company's ship department discussed the renaming of the ship with General Manager Liu. As a result of the discussion, it was decided to name it Haiyun (Sea Cloud) because it is operating to Lianyungang and is also a seagoing vessel. The captain and crew are also being considered. The company is also reporting to the Ministry of Communications, the Navigation Administration Bureau, and the Jianghai Customs to request registration and the issuance of a sailing license. It will then be deployed to the Shanghai-Lianyungang route as a regular service after the repairs are completed.

Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to Launch Tung Oil Loan Program; Zhejiang Construction Department to Send Personnel to Shanghai for Negotiations; General Bureau of Savings and Remittance Has Agreed to Allocate 100,000 Yuan

The China News Agency reports that the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department has stated that the Jinquchu areas of eastern Zhejiang are rich in tung oil, and the amount of oil produced and sold abroad each year is not small. Tung oil is a major export product. In order to relieve the farmers' economic hardship and improve production methods, in addition to ordering the counties that produce tung oil to organize cooperatives, it is also negotiating with the financial community to borrow large sums of money to launch a seedling loan program to provide farmers with capital to expand planting and fertilization. However, the counties that produce tung oil are located in remote areas, and most of them do not have financial institutions to handle the tung oil seedling loan program, which makes it very difficult. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau is planning to allocate funds to launch a rural loan program in order to promote the prosperity of the rural areas of Zhejiang Province, which may provide an opportunity for cooperative management. The department has specially sent Chen Zhongming, director of the Cooperative Management Office of the Agricultural Management Committee, from Hangzhou to Shanghai to negotiate cooperative arrangements with the person in charge of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. The results of the meeting were very satisfactory. The General Bureau of Savings and Remittance has agreed to allocate 100,000 yuan for the tung oil seedling loan program in Zhejiang Province, and the amount of loans will be distributed according to the amount of tung oil produced in each county. After further consultation, the contract can be formally signed. In order to actively proceed with the plan, the Construction Department has ordered the counties that produce tung oil to formulate loan plans and improvement plans. Currently, four or five counties have submitted their plans in compliance with the order. The Construction Department will determine the loan method after all the county plans have been submitted and will then transfer the loans to the farmers through the cooperatives.

No Genuine Cases of Cholera Have Occurred in This City

The Municipal Health Bureau issued a statement yesterday stating that the news report in the newspapers yesterday (the 18th) that two genuine cases of cholera had been discovered at the Hongkou Epidemic Hospital had attracted the attention of the Municipal Health Bureau. The bureau immediately sent personnel to the hospital to investigate. According to the hospital director, Wang Boyuan, no genuine cases of cholera had been discovered. However, two patients with vomiting had come to the hospital for treatment. Yesterday, a reporter from a news agency called to inquire whether any cholera patients had been discovered. The hospital staff informed the reporter that two patients had come to the hospital for treatment. The reporter mistakenly assumed that these two patients were cholera patients and issued the erroneous news report. The hospital will request a correction to avoid misrepresentation. The Municipal Health Bureau has strictly instructed the hospital to inform its staff that they should not casually release information about illnesses without scientific verification to avoid misleading the public.

According to yesterday's report, the draft was adopted from the East China News Agency. The correction letter is now compiled as follows:

Wu Liande wrote: Sir, I have read in today's newspaper that genuine cases of cholera have been discovered in the city. Our office attaches great importance to this matter. We have inquired with Dr. Lin Chunshan, the medical director of the Hongkou Epidemic Hospital, who stated that this is not the case. We request that you take steps to correct this information immediately. We have always admired your newspaper as a leader of public opinion. In the future, if you have any news about cholera, please inform our office first by telegram, and we will be happy to provide a sincere response. If the information is false, please do not publish it to avoid misleading the public. This letter is sent to you for your information and handling. Sincerely, Wu Liande, Chairman of the Shanghai Temporary Office for the Prevention of Cholera, July 18.

The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital wrote: Sir, we were shocked to read in the local news section of your newspaper on the 18th of this month that a genuine case of cholera had been discovered in the city. The number of people examined at our hospital as of yesterday was 1,226, not 452, and there were no cases of Lin Shixin or Li Chen's family suffering from genuine cholera. Moreover, the hospital's medical affairs are managed by Drs. Lin Chunshan and Zhu Xiaofang, and there is no director named Wang Boyuan. In addition, if a patient suffers from genuine cholera, it is impossible for them to be cured in the afternoon after being admitted to the hospital in the morning. It is clear that someone is spreading rumors with ulterior motives. This matter concerns the peace and security of the entire city, and it is urgent to clarify the truth. In addition to reporting this matter to the Municipal Health Bureau for investigation, we are sending this special letter to request a correction to clarify the facts. Sincerely, Hongkou Epidemic Hospital, July 18.

Regulations for the Presentation and Inspection of Ship Entry and Exit Documents; Customs Notice Amending Articles 7 and 9

Tang Haian, Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, and Luo Fude, Tax Commissioner, issue Joint Notice No. 1456 regarding the amendment of Articles 7 and 9 of the Regulations for the Presentation and Inspection of Ship Entry and Exit Documents. It states that the Regulations for the Presentation and Inspection of Ship Entry and Exit Documents were issued on September 19, 1934, under Notice No. 1384. Now, by order of the Ministry of Finance, Articles 7 and 9 of the Regulations for the Presentation and Inspection of Ship Entry and Exit Documents have been revised. The revised articles are copied below for compliance. It is hereby notified for the information of all merchants and shippers.

Revised Articles:

Article 7

If any goods not listed on the manifest are discovered by the Customs, the captain and the owner of the goods shall each be subject to a fine of between 200 and 2,000 yuan in national currency, and the goods may be confiscated. If two or more packages are combined into one without detailed notation on the manifest, or if the manifest lists the goods vaguely, the captain and the owner of the goods shall each be subject to a fine of up to 1,000 yuan in national currency. If any goods not listed on the manifest are hidden by special methods in an attempt to deceive the Customs, such as using shelves, secret compartments, permanent structures on the ship, or movable fixtures as hiding places, and are discovered by the Customs, in addition to confiscating the goods, the captain may be subject to a fine of up to 2,000 yuan in national currency for each hiding place, and the ship may be temporarily detained until the case is closed. If the captain can prove or the owner of the goods can prove that the captain was merely negligent and not complicit in the foregoing circumstances, and the circumstances are minor, excusable, or beyond the captain's control, the fine may be waived at the discretion of the authorities.

Article 9

When a Chinese-flagged ship enters port, the captain shall submit the following documents to the Customs for inspection at the time of submitting the manifest: Ship Entry Report, Ship Nationality Certificate, Ship Registration Certificate, Ship Route Certificate, Ship Inspection Certificate, Logbook, Ship Tax Payment Certificate (referring to ships that have paid ship tax and obtained a certificate), Ship Tonnage Certificate, List of Firearms for Self-Defense (two copies), Fumigation Certificate, List of Ship's Stores (see Article 11), Passenger List (see Article 10), Clearance Documents (referring to ships coming from Chinese trading ports). When a foreign-flagged ship enters port, the captain shall submit the following documents for inspection: Ship Entry Report, Ship Nationality Certificate, Ship Tax Payment Certificate (referring to ships that have paid ship tax and obtained a certificate), List of Firearms for Self-Defense (two copies), Fumigation Certificate, List of Ship's Stores (see Article 11), Passenger List (see Article 10), Clearance Documents (referring to ships coming from Chinese trading ports). Foreign ships entering port may be exempted from submitting a Ship Nationality Certificate to the Customs, provided that they submit an Entry Report signed by the Consul in charge, certifying that the original Ship Nationality Certificate has been deposited with the Consulate. However, if a foreign government does not allow Chinese ships trading in its domestic ports to deposit their Nationality Certificates with the Chinese Consulate, then ships of that country trading in China shall not enjoy this benefit.

Ministry of Industry to Revise Factory Registration Regulations; Unregistered Factories to Complete Procedures Within Six Months

The Shih She News Agency reports that the Factory Registration Regulations were formulated by the Ministry of Industry and promulgated for implementation in December 1931. However, the number of factories that have registered according to law is still small. It is now reported that the Ministry of Industry, in order to vigorously implement this work, has specially revised and published the original regulations and formulated a factory registration certificate form, ordering the Construction Department of each province and the Social Bureau of each city to comply. The revised registration regulations stipulate that all factories owned by Chinese citizens that regularly employ 30 or more workers or use mechanical power for manufacturing shall complete registration within six months of the promulgation of these regulations. Those who fail to register after the deadline may be punished in accordance with the Administrative Execution Law and ordered to complete registration. New factories that fail to apply for registration within two months will not be heard. After receiving the document, the Social Bureau of this city has formulated various forms and certificates in accordance with the law and issued them to various factories for registration. As the factory sites are located in busy urban areas, the noise and smoke generated often arouse the opposition of the general public. In order to protect industry, maintain social order, and take both sides into account, a separate Notification on the Management of Factory Site Addresses has been formulated and implemented last year. Existing factories are required to apply for permits within a prescribed period, and new factories must apply to the Social Bureau for approval before starting construction.

Foreigners' Association Advocates Reducing Rickshaws

The Great American Evening Post reports that the Foreigners' Association of this city recently passed six resolutions at a general meeting to address the issues of traffic noise and traffic congestion in Shanghai, urging the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement and the French Municipal Council to pay attention to these situations that tarnish Shanghai's glory. It advocates reducing the number of rickshaws by at least 10% each year, encouraging cheap transportation methods, increasing the number of traffic police, implementing uniform signals, and reducing inconvenience to pedestrians.

Interview with Telegraph Bureau Director Bao Keyong on the Communication Status in Flood-Stricken Areas; Wired Telegraph Slightly Affected, Wireless Telegraph Reporting Normally

In recent days, the river water has risen violently in various places along the Yangtze River, and wired telegraphs have been reported to be obstructed due to the collapse of telegraph poles. A reporter from the Central News Agency interviewed Mr. Bao Keyong, director of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, to inquire about the communication status in the flood-stricken areas. According to Mr. Bao, the volume of telegrams in Wuhan and Jiujiang is usually quite high. Although it is still possible to communicate during the floods, the time delay has become a problem. Shashi is also experiencing similar difficulties, but since the volume of telegrams is low, there is no significant impact. Wuhan and Jiujiang have always communicated directly, but now they have to detour through Zhengzhou, which also causes delays. As for wireless telegraphs, they are still reporting normally, even in the flood-stricken areas, and are not affected at all. However, due to the obstruction of wired telegraphs, the volume of telegrams has become quite congested.

(1) Report on the previous resolution; (2) Matters for discussion. A. How should we deal with the letter from the Business Resumption Committee requesting a postponement of the request for repayment? (Resolution) Reply to the committee that it must submit a detailed plan, procedure, and date for the resumption of business to the Union before the Union's Standing Committee meeting on the 21st of this month, before a decision is made on whether the Union's representatives should proceed with the request for repayment. The meeting adjourned at around 11:00 a.m.

Railway Department Revises Round-Trip Group Ticket Return Deadline

The Ministry of Railways yesterday instructed the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, stating: According to a report from the Ministry's Business Department, the 18th proposal of the 9th National Railway Transportation Conference, proposing amendments to Articles 40 (D) and (G) of the Passenger Train Transportation Regulations, was resolved by the conference in its 38th resolution, stating, "The first item is approved in principle, Article 40, Item D, of the Passenger Transportation Regulations is amended as requested, and the second item is reserved for reference," which is deemed feasible. Now, the stipulation in item (2) of that article, "Holders of round-trip group tickets shall have a validity period that is double the time of the slowest passenger train in the timetable, plus fifteen days, within which the return journey must be completed," should be revised to read: "Those purchasing group round-trip tickets must declare the return period when purchasing the ticket, but from the date of purchase to the date of arrival at the starting station, the period must not exceed two months. Overdue tickets will be void and no extension can be requested." In addition to separate orders, you are hereby ordered to comply with this order. It is understood that the Railway Administration has instructed the Traffic Department to comply accordingly.

Lawyers Association Admonishes Lawyers to Compete in Self-Reflection and Mutual Improvement

The Republic of China Lawyers Association issued a notice to lawyers' associations in various provinces, stating: This is for the purpose of notification. The lawyer system, in modern civilized countries, has a duty to utilize the law to eliminate the contradictions accumulated in human real life, or to resolve the obvious struggles in human real life. In other words, it is to integrate people's real life with the law, thereby forming a path of common compliance and establishing a foundation of social trust. However, those who are not fully educated, have questionable conduct, tarnish the reputation, and are criticized by the world, also exist. This is undeniable. The Association looks outward and feels anxious. It believes that lawyers in our country today should be loyal servants who love and protect the law, and vanguards who protect human rights. The responsibilities are so solemn. However, due to a small number of colleagues who have disgraced their duties and tarnished their reputation, giving people reasons for criticism, and damaging the entire profession, every time it is thought of, it is with great regret. Recently, judicial officials have admonished legal professionals with extreme severity, and the earnestness of rectification overflows from their words. Our lawyers are one of the three major judicial professions. How can we not feel ashamed? Despite the many shortcomings of this writing, in order to uphold the principles of self-respect and autonomy, it offers advice that is unpleasant to the ear but beneficial to practice. It is hoped that all members of our associations, from now on, will break through considerations of personal relationships, seriously investigate all members, and strive to compete in self-reflection and mutual improvement, thinking about how to establish a model for the future and how to wash away the stains of the past, being vigilant against selfish desires for material things, and spontaneously generating a sense of justice. The impact will not only allow the legal profession to restore its inherent glory, but also benefit the people and the country.

Chinese Buddhist Association National Representative Conference Resolves That Non-Members May Not Serve as Heads of Temples, Requests a Strict Prohibition of Troops Stationing in Monasteries, Closing Tonight

The Chinese Buddhist Association held its National Representative Conference at 9:00 AM yesterday on Hart Road, scheduled to close tonight. Details are as follows:

Representative Conference

Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, the Association held its 7th National Representative Conference at 418 Hart Road. Over a hundred people attended, including Liaofan, Lei Zhuohuan, Baosheng, and Pan Zhongqing from Hunan; Huang Jianyu, Rongxu, and Benseng from Anhui; Kuanda, Qu Wenliu, and Li Lianhou from Shanghai; Dabei and Yuelai from Hubei; Xingyuan, Ruijin, Mingjue, and Kuanrun from Fujian; Zhenkong and Dalin from Henan; Xijing from Jiangxi; Zhu'an, Huai Kun, Bingling, and Songyue; Chan Ding, Benzhi, Jieming, Kongchao, and Ningyuanjian from Sichuan; Faquan, Zhiguang, Zhenzong, Jimu, Yihe, Zhengdao, and Liaoxing from Jiangsu; Qian Chunyi, Zhou Baiming, and Ma Muyan from Shandong; Fucheng, Miaoji, and Ruyu from Nanjing; Qiu Zhaotao, Chang Shichang, Shengyi, Yu Shenlian, Shenghui, and Hu Mengzi from Zhejiang. Mao Yun, a representative from the Central People's Movement Committee and the Municipal Party Department, and Hong Kui, a representative from the Ministry of Interior and the Municipal Government, attended to guide the meeting.

Resolutions

The conference publicly elected Qu Yingguang, Yuanying, Dabei, Zhiyuan, and Huang Hanzhi as the presidium. After performing the rituals, Yuanying first reported the number of representatives attending from each province, followed by the secretariat's report on the general affairs and financial situation of the sixth session. Subsequently, Mao Yun, Hong Kui, and Zhang Bing delivered speeches one after another, mainly encouraging unity, organizational soundness, to promote Buddhist studies, and to benefit the country and society. Then, the discussion of proposals began. It was resolved: 1. To approve the constitution; 2. That non-members may not serve as heads of temples; 3. To promote monks engaging in productive activities; 4. To order the Shanghai Buddhist Association to handle the accommodation of beggar monks; 5. To send personnel to guide Buddhist associations at all levels; 6. To establish a Buddhist Compassion Relief Association; 7. To order Buddhist associations at all levels to conduct literacy education; 8. To submit a request to the Military Affairs Commission to issue a nationwide order strictly prohibiting troops from stationing in Buddhist temples; 9. Strict prohibition of troops stationing in monasteries and scenic spots. Other proposals will be discussed further today, and executive supervisors will be re-elected. The conference will close tonight.

Before the Xinwei Relief Society, a Large Number of Refugees Seek Boat Tickets; the Society Declines Due to Financial Reasons

Shanghai's economy is depressed, factories are closed, workers are unemployed, and the number of people from disaster areas in various provinces coming to Shanghai to make a living is increasing daily. Therefore, making a living is difficult, and drifting at sea is pitiful. Yesterday afternoon around 3:00 PM, more than two hundred refugees gathered at the entrance of the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road. They were repeatedly dispersed, but they returned again and again, pleading with the Xinwei Relief Society to issue free boat tickets. However, the Society, due to the large number of vagrants in the area who seize the opportunity to mix among them, obtain boat tickets, and then sell them, while genuine refugees are unable to obtain relief, and also because of limited finances, had already issued a notice to stop issuing free tickets. It was unable to meet the demands of the refugees. Unexpectedly, the refugees were numerous and noisy and refused to leave, waiting at the door until 8:00 PM before dispersing reluctantly.

Cai Fei, Seeking a Magic Cure, Suddenly Hit by a Stray Bullet

Cai Ronggen, 35 years old, a local resident of No. 35, opposite the Nanxin Bridge Cement Factory on Longhua Road, Nanshi, his wife, Cai Fei, 30 years old, from Longhua, because their son was ill, Cai's wife Fei, accompanied by a woman named Cai Linzhen, went to Longhua Temple to offer incense and seek a magic cure for their son's illness. Therefore, around 9:00 AM yesterday, while walking through the intersection of Xiaomu Bridge Road on Longhua Road, suddenly a stray bullet flew over and hit Cai Fei's left lower abdomen. She immediately fell to the ground in extreme pain. Her companion, Cai Linzhen, reported the incident to the Second Defense Office of the nearby Security Corps, but they refused to accept the case, instructing her to report to the Public Security Bureau for handling. Subsequently, the woman hired a rickshaw and sent the injured Cai Fei to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. Because the hospital examined Fei's abdomen for bullets, but no family members were at the hospital to take responsibility, the bullets could not be removed. Fortunately, she was still conscious and there was probably no danger to her life. The incident was learned by the Ximen Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, which immediately dispatched a detective team led by Squad Leader Shen Wenda, Foremen Fang Lin, and detectives Bian Wenguang to investigate. They investigated where the bullet came from and injured the person, and also investigated nearby military and police units, but there was no live ammunition target practice. Director Li still ordered detectives to investigate for verification and ordered Shanghai Hospital to find a way to quickly remove the bullet from the woman's abdomen to save her life.

French Concession Establishes Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Branch, Clinic Already Open

The National News Agency reporter made a special trip to the newly established Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Branch on Beile Road in the French Concession of this port. An official of the Association, Mr. Yan, led a visit to the various departments: the Rickshaw Pullers Clinic, Dispensing Room, Classroom, Storytelling Room, Broadcasting Room, Bathroom, Dormitory, etc. Currently, due to the hot weather, the clinic is already open. Other parts are still under internal renovation, and will be implemented step by step after the work is completed. It is said that the Association headquarters shows educational films every Sunday to improve the knowledge of rickshaw pullers.

French Concession Wood Industry Opposes Sanitation Tax, Writes to Various Groups Seeking Abolition

There are forty to fifty wood businesses in the French Concession of this port. Two years ago, the French Concession Public Works Bureau notified the wood businesses to donate for a classified business sanitation license. The wood businesses, having been established for many years without this sanitation tax, could not accept it and unanimously expressed opposition. They jointly wrote to the Fourth District Branch of the Second Special District Citizens Association of this city, asking them to forward it to the Chinese Taxpayers Association of the French Concession to argue with the Public Works Bureau, and the result was that the donation license was waived. Unexpectedly, this month, the wood businesses suddenly received a written notice from the Classified Business Office of the French Public Works Bureau stating that from now on, they should donate a classified business license to the bureau and pay an examination fee of two or ten yuan. Upon receiving the notice, the wood businesses were panicked and said that they had firmly opposed the extra donation by the bureau two years ago, and they had already negotiated its cancellation. Moreover, at a time when the market is depressed and industries are declining, they were really unable to bear it. They jointly wrote to the Second Special District Citizens Association, the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association, and the trade association of this city yesterday, requesting that they make a strong case. At the same time, they are also starting to organize a temporary office for the wood industry trade association of the French Concession, in order to unite and fight to the end.

Overview of the Public Concession's Suppression of Narcotics

According to the report of the Public Concession Police Department for June, the patrol unit continued to seriously suppress opium and narcotics within the concession. A total of eleven reports of searches were obtained by the Central Police Station, and forty-one opium offenders were arrested. A total of one hundred and ten cases were searched by various police stations, and three hundred and forty-one offenders were arrested. A total of one hundred and twenty-nine opium offenders were sentenced to imprisonment, of which forty-five were also fined. A total of one hundred and eighty-nine were only fined. Five were transferred to the Chinese territory, one was warned, one lawsuit was withdrawn, fifty-five were reprimanded, and two were detained. The narcotics seized on that day included 197 taels of opium, over 170 taels of opium substitutes, over 2 taels of morphine, 81 taels of heroin, and 215 items of opium pipes and morphine needles. The total amount of fines paid by various opium offenders this month was 14,830 yuan and 20 Japanese yen.

Public Concession Crime Statistics for June

According to the report of the Acting Chief Superintendent of the Public Concession Police Department for June, a total of 1,240 crime cases were reported this month, a decrease of 193 cases compared to May, but an increase of 124 cases compared to the same month last year. The main reason for the increase is the large number of petty theft cases. If we consider the number of criminals arrested, there were only 1,252 people this month, which is not a decrease compared to April and May. In addition, there were 144 people who committed crimes in previous months but were only arrested in June, and 67 people were arrested on behalf of other local authorities. If we classify the crimes by type, there were 24 cases of armed robbery, 25 cases of burglary, 23 cases of home robbery, and 19 cases of shop robbery (18 arrests), 72 cases of petty theft (59 arrests), 6 cases of receiving stolen goods, and 49 cases of snatching. The vehicles reported stolen included two cars and 49 bicycles. Two cars and 17 bicycles were recovered. The total value of stolen property reported this month was over 150,070 yuan. The total value of stolen property reported last month was only slightly less than 72,000 yuan. The reason for the increase this month is that one case involved the embezzlement and misuse of over 65,000 yuan of public funds. The total value of recovered property this month was over 27,000 yuan. In June, 20 men and 15 women reported suicides to the police. Four communist criminals were arrested this month, one was released on bail, and the remaining 30 were still in custody. A total of 1,268 communist books were seized. Furthermore, there were two factory strikes in the Public Concession in June, affecting a total of 1,514 workers. The time lost due to work stoppages totaled 32,592 days.

Ye Jiaxing and Others Suggest Transferring Ritual Funds to Disaster Relief, Yesterday Sent Letters to Various Groups for Submission to the Central Government

Ye Jiaxing, a member of the Commercial Research Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Ye Ping, a secretary of the Social Affairs Bureau, in view of the extreme severity of floods in various places and the widespread misery, yesterday sent letters to various groups in this city, requesting that they be submitted to the Central Government, ordering all provinces and cities across the country to transfer the funds for folk rituals to disaster relief, so as to achieve real benefits. The original letter stated: "We are writing to you because since the beginning of summer this year, floods have caused disasters in various places, mountain floods have broken out, and rivers have overflowed. In addition, continuous rain has caused water levels to increase sharply. The provinces of Shandong, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Hunan, and Jiangxi have all suffered great calamities. Bridges have been washed away, dams have collapsed, autumn crops have been submerged, and houses have been swept away. Wherever the floods have reached, nothing has been left behind. Hundreds of counties, large and small, have become swamps. The area of the disaster area is estimated to be over one million square li, and the number of compatriots affected has reached twenty to thirty million. Misery is everywhere, and they are crying for food. The severity of the disaster is almost the same as that in the 20th year of the Republic of China. Now, the authorities in various provinces are urgently providing relief, or engaging in rescue operations, or allocating relief funds. Even if it is a drop in the bucket, it can save one in a thousand or a hundred. However, recently, it has been reported that superstitious people in the interior are even collecting money to perform rituals to pray for disaster relief. To waste useful money on useless purposes is a great waste of money and labor. Considering that when the flood disaster was extremely severe in the 20th year of the Republic of China, there were no rituals performed in various places, and now the disaster has reappeared, it is clear that they are of no practical help. Moreover, our country today has reached the extreme of economic collapse. Every expenditure must be worth one yuan's equivalent, so that there is no waste of money and the people receive real benefits. Jiaxing and others, in view of this, hereby request that you jointly forward this to the Central Government, ordering the various provinces and cities to instruct the various county governments that if there are folk rituals that collect money, the funds should be transferred to repairing embankments, controlling water, and providing post-disaster relief in the disaster area, so that all people will benefit deeply."

Wind and Rain Yesterday Morning and Evening, Heat Wave in This Port Slightly Reduced, Hailstorm for Several Minutes Around 3:00 PM, South Pacific Typhoon Now Moving Northwest

The weather in this city has been hot recently, especially the previous two days. Therefore, summer epidemics have been successively discovered. Yesterday, due to wind and rain in the morning and evening, the heat wave has slightly subsided. Details are as follows:

Morning and Evening Wind and Rain

The heat wave in this port has been very high recently, all around 100 degrees. The previous two days, due to the heat and sultriness, many summer epidemics were discovered. Yesterday morning around 2:00 AM, there was a rainstorm with thunder. At 5:15 AM at dawn, a strong southeast wind rose again. Therefore, the temperature before noon reached a maximum of 91.05 degrees Fahrenheit. At 2:00 PM, it rose to over 94 degrees. At 3:35 PM, the weather suddenly turned cloudy and clear, with thunder booming. Hail fell for four or five minutes, followed by showers. It stopped at 4:15 PM. A gentle breeze blew, and the weather quickly cleared. Therefore, the heat wave was less intense than the previous day.

Beneficial to Crops

Since the beginning of summer in this port, the weather has been very moderate. Although the Yangtze River flood is severe, it has not been affected in any way. Even Songjiang, Jinshan, Qingpu, Jiading, and Baoshan counties near Shanghai have neither shallow rivers nor high water levels. Therefore, irrigation for crops is very suitable. Although the heat has been high for a week, there has been a rainstorm every day. According to farmers, the climate during this summer is very beneficial to agricultural products.

Boatman Killed by Lightning

In the past two days, the weather has been extremely hot and abnormal. The thermometer reading is often above 100 degrees, and showers fall from time to time. Yesterday (the 18th) morning, the weather was still sultry. Around 4:00 PM, the weather suddenly changed, with dark clouds gathering, lightning flashing, thunder rumbling, and heavy rain pouring. Suddenly, a thunderclap struck. There were six boatmen inside a lighter docked at Dongjiabo Litu in the south of Shanghai, all sheltering from the rain in the cabin. Upon hearing the sound of thunder, they all fainted in shock. After a while, the boatmen woke up and checked the number of people. Only five people were left. One of them, a certain person, was missing. While they were wondering, they suddenly heard a commotion on the shore. The boatmen went ashore to check and found that a certain person had been struck to death at the north side of the Dongjiabo pier, kneeling on both feet, shirtless, with the skin on his chest scorched by lightning, his hair also burnt and curled, and his cloth pants unburnt. His head was burnt and his face was swollen, and his death was terrible. For a while, the onlookers blocked the road.

High Tide in This City This Morning, Yesterday's Tide Exceeded Forecast

A high tide was detected in this city starting at 2:05 AM this morning. Due to the northeast wind last night, the height may exceed the 11 feet 7 inches record forecast by the Whangpoo Conservancy Board. At 1:50 AM yesterday morning, the Whangpoo Bureau water level record (Suzhou Creek Estuary) had reached 11 feet 2.2 inches, 8 inches higher than the forecast of 11 feet 6.2 inches. At 2:00 PM, it had exceeded 12 feet. Last night, the night tide began at 11:35 PM, and the peak was at 1:21 AM this morning. The highest tide was at 1:26 AM. This morning, the highest tide started to rise at 12:19 AM, and the rush was from 1:20 AM to the highest tide at 2:05 AM. Since it coincided with the collision of incoming and outgoing tides, the rise will exceed the forecast.

The Hurricane in the South Pacific is Still Advancing, Whether it Will Hit Shanghai is Still Unknown, Hurricane Center Reaches 120 Nautical Miles

The hurricane discovered in the South Pacific is now moving northwest. According to the report from the observatory yesterday morning, the hurricane has now blown to 126 degrees east longitude and 19 degrees north latitude, approximately northeast of Luzon. The center of the wind force is 120 nautical miles, so the wind is very strong. The direction is northwest. Whether it will hit Shanghai is still uncertain because it is far from Shanghai. The hurricane is moving fast. The morning before yesterday, it was still hovering between 130 degrees east longitude and 3 degrees north latitude. In one day, the difference in latitude and longitude reached five or six degrees.

The police stations in charge sent detectives to transport the bodies to the Feilun Road morgue for investigation. Details are as follows: (1) The Xinzha Police Station reported the male body of Shi Huanzhong, from Beiping, 58 years old, living at No. 12 Baiyu Lane, Laborbert Road, working as a gatekeeper at No. 769 Xiude New Village, Chengdu Road. At 3:30 PM the day before yesterday, just as he was on duty, he suddenly collapsed from heatstroke. After someone reported it to the police station, an ambulance was called, and he was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died at 10:50 PM that night. (2) The Jiaxing Road Police Station investigated the female body of Xu Wang, from Ningbo, 64 years old, whose son worked as a boatman, living at No. 110 Oujia Road. Around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, the old woman went out for business and collapsed from heatstroke on the road at the Xinjibang Road intersection of Zhoujiazhui Road. After being found by the police, she was sent to Shanghai Sanatorium for treatment, but it was ineffective. She died at 4:30 AM yesterday morning. (3) The Yulin Road Police Station reported an unidentified male body, about 50 years old, resembling a coolie, who was found by the police at 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, collapsing from heatstroke on the side of Huishan Road, Huasheng Road. Ministry of Finance Sets Reporting Measures to Reward Seizure of Smuggling, Strictly Prevent Smuggling and Tax Evasion by奸商, Rewards for Customs Officers and Informants After Seizure

In order to prevent the奸商 from evading taxes and smuggling, the Ministry of Finance has formulated four measures for issuing bonuses for seizing smuggling ships, and has notified the customs to know. The measures are as follows: (1) Whenever the customs seizes a smuggling vessel in operation, or seizes smuggling civilian ships, sailing ships, sampans, etc., when the customs dismantles them, it should follow the current profit-sharing method, and auction the ship. Half of the value that can be obtained (up to a limit of 1,000 yuan), or the total number of dismantled parts that can be converted into money, whichever is higher. As for informant bonuses, they can only be calculated based on the total number of separately converted parts. (2) Whenever the customs seizes a smuggling vessel operated by machine, with a registered tonnage of less than 100 tons, or seizes smuggling civilian ships, sailing ships, sampans, etc., when the customs converts them for use as patrol boats, the customs should purchase them at half of the value that can be obtained from the auction of the ship (up to a limit of 1,000 yuan). The bonuses for the officers and informants will be calculated according to the purchase price. (3) Whenever the customs, after reporting to the Inspector General of Customs and verifying it, disposes of it in other ways (such as selling it to government agencies, etc.), the amount of bonuses issued to customs officers and informants shall be determined by the Inspector General of Customs. (4) Whenever the customs seizes a smuggling vessel operated by machine, with a registered tonnage of 100 tons or more, and the customs converts it for use as a patrol boat, or sells it with the approval of the Inspector General of Customs, the price at which the customs purchases the ship, and the amount of bonuses for customs officers and informants, shall be determined by the Inspector General of Customs.

Wusong Broadcasting Station Officially Starts Construction, Broadcasting to be Completed Within This Year

The International Telecommunications Bureau, following the order of the Ministry of Communications, is setting up a radio broadcasting station in Shanghai. The address has been surveyed and determined to be near the Wusong Fort Taiwan. The power is 1,000 kilowatts, making it the second largest broadcasting station in the country. The total cost is approximately 500,000 yuan. There are two antenna iron towers, 100 meters high and 40 tons heavy, which have been contracted by merchants and officially started construction last week. It is expected to be completed within this year. All the machinery has been ordered from abroad and has already been shipped to Shanghai. Once the antenna iron towers are installed, a broadcasting room will be set up on the top floor of the International Hotel or Sassoon House, and broadcasting will begin.

Victim of Automobiles - Only Three Deaths Last Month - Lowest in Over Five Years

According to the Police Department's report for June, there were 2,029 reported cases of bicycle violations. Among them, 608 cases were prosecuted in various courts, including 96 cases involving foreigners and 512 cases involving Chinese. The remaining cases were handled with warnings and registration of the offenses based on the severity of the violation. In the same month, the Central and Lao Zha police stations investigated a total of 1,597 cases of public rickshaw violations of traffic regulations. Eighteen privately-owned chartered cars had their licenses revoked for soliciting business. There were 47 cases of automobiles abusing their horns, resulting in penalties. One chauffeur, repeatedly violating the law without repentance, had his license revoked. In June of this year, the number of deaths caused by traffic accidents was only three, which is the lowest number since February 1930. The total number of incidents, including injuries and property damage, was 729. Further analysis reveals 75 incidents involving both property damage and injuries (two deaths), 415 incidents involving only property damage, and 239 incidents involving only injuries (one death).

Second Special Court - Prison Riot Erupts - Bowls and Chamber Pots Thrown Everywhere - Offenders Sent to Police Station for Interrogation

In the heavy crime section of the detention center of the Second Special District Court, prisoners awaiting appeal for crimes such as murder and robbery suddenly started arguing over a trivial matter at 11:00 AM yesterday. The argument quickly escalated into mutual insults and physical altercations, with cries for help reaching the outside. The prisoners even threw bowls and chamber pots, leaving the prison cell and corridor littered with broken pieces of bowls and human waste. The guards on duty were unable to stop them. The detention center immediately reported the incident to the Central Police Station in Lujiawan. A large group of Chinese and foreign detectives, led by the Western Section Chief and a detective supervisor from the Police Department, arrived and quelled the disturbance after about half an hour. The prisoners involved in the riot were identified as Li Guochen (the mastermind behind a murder case in a hotel, originally sentenced to death, appealed to the Supreme Court, and sent back for retrial, recently resentenced to life imprisonment by the Third Branch of the High Court), Li Shiying (a key suspect in the assassination of Wang Bin and Cao Qingcheng, inspectors of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau of the Shanghai Garrison Headquarters, originally sentenced to death, appealed to the Supreme Court, sent back for retrial, still maintaining the original sentence, currently still appealing), Tao Yongchang (a key suspect in the assassination of Cao Adi, originally sentenced to 15 years in prison, recently extorted money from Wang Xinggao, a fellow prisoner, prosecuted by the Police Department and sentenced to another six months in prison, both cases are currently on appeal), Wang Deyu (killed his cousin Ding Fugen in an attempt to seize property, originally sentenced to death, currently appealing to the Supreme Court, recently acquitted in the extortion case against Wang Xinggao), and Lu Bujiang, Chen Dekuan, Chen Yonggui, Liu Quansheng, and Jin Changfa, who were involved in robbery, theft, and drug-related cases. The nine prisoners were taken to the police station for interrogation. When the prisoners were brought out, Li Guocheng and Wang Deyu were bleeding from head wounds caused by the beating. They were supported by police officers and bailiffs, appearing to be severely injured. It is rumored that the cause of the riot was that Li Guocheng, while in detention, wanted the other prisoners to acknowledge him as the "old boss" and extorted 30 yuan in "protection money." The prisoners refused to obey, leading to the argument and fighting. The veracity of this account remains to be verified.

Monk Commits Suicide by Drowning - Eight Pawn Tickets Found Nearby

The body of a monk who committed suicide by drowning was discovered off the coast of Baotai in Wusong the day before yesterday. Yesterday, the Wusong Life Saving Bureau's patrol boat recovered the body. The monk, wearing a cotton robe, appeared to be around 50 years old and a traveling monk from elsewhere. It is speculated that this follower of Buddha, who should have been detached from worldly affairs, was somehow moved to commit suicide. A certificate from the Fushou Monastery in Hanzhou, Sichuan, identifying the monk as Puyue from Jiangning, Jiangsu, was found on his person. Eight pawn tickets were also found, suggesting that he had pawned everything and was driven to take his own life. The charitable organization is preparing the coffin and burial.

Strange and Beautiful Spider - Black Web with White English Letters

Ge Baosheng, a mail carrier at the Wusong Post Office, is a hardworking old mailman, 50 years of age, from Jiangwan. His house is at number 13, Lane 23, behind the main street of Xisong Xing Road. Opposite his house is a bamboo fence, at the base of which he planted one or two pumpkins. The pumpkin vines wound around the top of the fence. In the middle of the vines, he suddenly discovered a strange and beautiful spider five days ago, completely different from ordinary spiders. The spider's body is about the size of a broad bean, with six particularly long legs. Its flat, round body is a purplish-brown color with three light golden yellow lines. The head is white with a beautiful silky sheen. The back four legs are black, and the front two legs are shaped like shrimp pincers with glossy black and white feathers covering them, making it pleasing to the eye. Most strangely, the spider web has four strands of white English letter-like shapes, each about an inch long, arranged at the tips of the four legs, which are very delicate and rare. It is specially recorded here for the study of entomologists.

Xinhua Bank Robbery Verdict - Wang Zhitin Sentenced to Eight Years, Zhu Paoyan Fined 300

On the morning of the 4th of last month, at about 10 a.m., three robbers armed with weapons broke into the Xinhua Bank branch on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. They stole 4,766.70 yuan in cash and fled. They opened fire in the Hehe Lane to resist arrest, killing a female servant and wounding Xue Guoxun, a gatekeeper of the lane. They fled to Chongqing Road in the International Settlement and killed a passerby. As a result, one of the robbers, Wang Zhitin from Anhui, 20 years old, was arrested at number 27, Ma'an Lane, Chongqing Road. A pistol was found on him and taken to the French Police Station. It was discovered that the pistol belonged to Zhu Paoyan, a native of Ningbo, who lived at number 31, Continental Apartments, Rue Luban, and was the general secretary of the Yi Minghua Bank. Zhu was arrested and the case was transferred to the Second Special District Court. The Police Department lawyer prosecuted Wang for robbery and murder and Zhu for violating the regulations on the prohibition of military firearms. These details have been reported in previous newspapers. The case has been investigated and concluded, and the verdict was delivered yesterday. At 9 a.m., Judge Sun Pengham and Clerk Tao Zongkan from the Second Special Court arrived at the First Criminal Court. Wang Zhitin was found guilty of armed robbery in collusion with others and sentenced to eight years in prison. He was found not guilty of the murder charge. Zhu Paoyan was fined 300 yuan, and the pistol was confiscated. Wang was detained in the detention center pending appeal, and Zhu remained on bail of 3,000 yuan.

Police Request Ban on Publication of "New Life Weekly" - Petition to Court to Issue Ban Expected to be Decided Today

Because "New Life Weekly" published an article titled "Chatting About the Emperor," which contained slander against the Emperor of Japan, Zheng Yue, the Chief Prosecutor of the First Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, filed a public prosecution against Du Chongyuan, the editor and publisher of the journal. The Criminal Court of the court ruled that Du be sentenced to one year and two months in prison, and he has already been sent to prison. It has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper that the legal department of the Municipal Council, although the magazine had been banned from selling, there was no explicit ban on publication. Therefore, yesterday morning, the police lawyer Ru Baoyi filed a petition with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The written application stated that the "New Life Weekly" has been ordered by the court to ban the sale of the magazine, but there is no explicit provision for prohibiting its publication. Therefore, according to Article 41, paragraph 1 of the Publishing Law, they request the court to issue an order prohibiting the publication of "New Life Weekly" in order to facilitate compliance. Judge Yu Huating, along with Judges Zhou and Xiao and Prosecutor Zhong, presided over the First Criminal Court. After the police lawyer Ru clarified the reasons for the request, Judge Yu announced that the matter would be reviewed again today.

Municipal Council - Reorganization of the Orchestra - Committee Proposes Dissolution and Reorganization - Board Decides to Retain Until Next Year

The Municipal Council, with the intention of saving expenses, previously discussed reorganizing the existing Municipal Council Orchestra. This matter was referred to the Music Committee for detailed review. The questions were whether the existing Municipal Council Orchestra should be reorganized to save money and whether an organization should be retained that was similar to the existing organization. The sub-committee prepared a report stating that there was a real need to seek savings in the orchestra's expenses, as the orchestra's expenses reached 278,500 yuan last year, not including the cost of renting the concert hall and office. Therefore, the Music Committee proposed disbanding the existing orchestra and forming a new orchestra. The sub-committee drafted a plan for organizing the new orchestra, suggesting that after the new orchestra was established (excluding concert hall rent), the expenses would not exceed 200,000 yuan, thus saving 78,500 yuan per year. The four points suggested by the sub-committee are briefly summarized as follows: (1) The Municipal Council should retain an orchestra of the same size as the current one, but at a lower cost. (2) The Board of Directors should automatically disband the existing orchestra. The contracts of all musicians who have received letters of appointment should be terminated immediately. Those who are temporarily employed should be given one month's notice of termination and dismissed at the same time as the musicians with letters of appointment. (3) The date of disbandment should be decided by the Board of Directors, as the issue of disbanding the orchestra may require a decision by the taxpayers at the next annual meeting. (4) After the current orchestra is disbanded, a new orchestra should be organized immediately. Salaries should be calculated according to grade and should not enjoy the various benefits enjoyed by other employees of the Municipal Council. Contracts should be limited to one year but may be renewed annually. The organizational outline includes one director, one deputy director, one military music instructor, and 44 musicians. After detailed discussion, the Music Committee unanimously agreed to disband the existing orchestra and proposed organizing a new orchestra according to the plan prepared by the sub-committee. However, the timing of the dissolution still needs careful consideration. According to the Acting Director General, the existing orchestra should be retained until April of next year, after the taxpayers' annual meeting, so that taxpayers can freely decide (1) to dissolve it completely, (2) to retain the existing orchestra, or (3) to organize a new orchestra. The Director of Finance also agreed with the Acting Director General's proposal, advocating that April 30 of the following year be set as the expiration date of the orchestra members' contracts. After repeated discussions by the members, the suggestions of the sub-committee were slightly revised and submitted to the Board of Directors. The Board of Directors discussed the above proposals for a long time. According to the Board of Directors, (1) the future of the Municipal Council Orchestra should not be decided by the Board of Directors, but should be handled by the taxpayers as in the past. (2) After the taxpayers decide in the future, whether to completely disband or reorganize, the Board of Directors, in order to facilitate rapid implementation, should set the expiration date of the current musicians' contracts as close as possible to the date of the taxpayers' annual meeting. (3) May 31 of the following year seems to be an appropriate time. (4) The reorganization plan proposed by the Music Committee should be submitted to the taxpayers. Subsequently, the Board of Directors unanimously passed the following resolutions: (1) The future of the Municipal Council Orchestra should be submitted to the next taxpayers' annual meeting. (2) The Board of Directors should notify the musicians holding letters of appointment of the termination of their contracts. The musicians who are temporarily employed should be given one month's notice of termination and dismissed at the same time as the musicians holding letters of appointment. (3) The date of this dismissal is set for May 31, 1936. (4) If the taxpayers advocate retaining an orchestra of the same size as the current one, the orchestra should be organized according to the outline prepared by the sub-committee of the Music Committee. At this point, the much-debated question of the existence of the Municipal Council Orchestra has temporarily come to an end, pending the decision of the Western expatriate taxpayers' annual meeting next April.

Fire at Yunfei Automobile Paint Shop

At about 8:20 AM yesterday, a fire broke out in the paint shop of the Yunfei Automobile Corporation at 601 Yidingpan Road in West Shanghai. Painters Xu Xingsheng and coppersmith Bao Fa were repairing cars and repainting them for customers. Due to the hot weather, the spraying torch ignited a gasoline can next to the car, causing dense smoke and flames to shoot out of the roof. The Caojiadu Fire Brigade from the nearby police station was the first to arrive and put out the fire, followed by the Jing'an Temple Fire Brigade. The paint shop was completely destroyed, and Xu and Bao were badly burned on their limbs due to the gasoline splattering on their clothing. They were taken to the hospital by the company's car for treatment. It is reported that the loss is more than 20,000 yuan and fire insurance had been purchased.

New Methods for Cooling Off on City Ferry

The weather has been extremely hot these days, with people sweating profusely. The evenings are especially stifling, making it uncomfortable to stay at home. In light of this, the city ferry has been operating late-night cooling services, which have been extremely crowded with tourists. For those who have official duties and want to cool off in the evening but should not return home too late to avoid affecting their work the next day, here are two cooling off methods: (1) After work hours, at 5 or 6 PM, take the city ferry to Gaoqiao, then take a public bus directly to the beach. You can swim and bathe as you please. The bathing area has a large cafeteria with exquisite Western food, various cold drinks, and Yangzhou dim sum at very affordable prices. After dinner, rest and walk along the beach under the moonlight, feeling refreshed. Leave the beach at 5:40, take the bus to the pier, and take a special ferry back to Shanghai, arriving at the Beijing Road pier at 11 PM. (2) After finishing work, take a bath at home and have dinner at the waterfront restaurant at 7 PM. The restaurant overlooks the Huangpu River, making it extremely cool and free of mosquitoes. Linger for an hour or two, enjoying the moonlight and the shimmering waves, which add to the serenity. At 8:30, take the late-night cooling ferry to Gaoqiao or Wusong, returning to Shanghai at 12:30. Several hours of refreshing leisure will wash away all the noise and bustle.

Case of Two Women Contending for Child - Still No Solution - Examination Results Indicate Both Have the Possibility of Bearing Children - The Court Must Still Investigate and Interrogate

Chen Zhou, the wife of the late real estate tycoon Chen Yide, who lived at 260 Route Belles in the French Concession, was recently sued in the civil court of the Second Special District Court by Chen Yipei, Chen's concubine, who lived at 2, Jiusi Lane, Rue Puech, seeking a ruling to return her biological son, Chen Xiongguan (also known as Xiongyi). After several court hearings and summonses, because both plaintiffs claimed that Xiongguan was their own biological son, the presiding judge stated that unless scientific methods of examination were used, it would be insufficient to prove who Chen Xiongguan was born to. Therefore, he ordered both parties and Chen Xiongguan to be sent to the Zhenru Forensic Research Institute for examination to make a final decision. This has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. The Forensic Research Institute, based on the appearance, physique, and blood of the plaintiff Chen Yipei, the defendant Chen Zhou, and Chen Xiongguan, conducted a detailed examination and concluded that both Chen Yipei and Chen Zhou had the possibility of bearing Chen Xiongguan. They determined that Chen Xiongguan's age was between eight and twelve years old. They also verified that Chen Zhou had been pregnant and given birth. They have reported the details to the court. Yesterday morning, at 10:30 AM, Judge Ma reopened the civil case in the Seventh Court. The plaintiff's lawyer was present, and the defendant was represented by a lawyer. The court asked the plaintiff if they had received the appraisal report from the Forensic Research Institute and that the examination fee of 43 yuan would be borne equally by both parties and the plaintiff should pay it promptly. The court also asked if there was any other evidence to present. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the plaintiff was in financial straits and could pay the fee within days. The lawyer also requested an investigation that the plaintiff stated the child was born in July 1926, while the defendant stated the child was born in October 1925. If the child was indeed born to the defendant, then Chen Yide should have requested registration with the Catholic Church. This is a regulation in the Catholic Church that the birth of a child must be registered with the year, month, day, and time of birth. The defendant's lawyer retorted that the burden of proof was on the plaintiff, but the plaintiff could not prove whether they had cohabited with Chen Yide, or whether they had conceived and given birth during the cohabitation period, so how could they have this child out of thin air? The plaintiff Chen Xing had died young, and if she were still alive, she would be 15 or 16 years old, definitely not the current Chen Xiongguan. The court examined the statements and then ordered that the case be investigated further and summoned again at a later date.

Taxpayers' Association Appeals for Exemption from Tax Increase for "Tada" Cart Industry

The Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association yesterday sent a letter to the Municipal Council, which reads as follows: "Dear Sirs, We have received a letter from the Shanghai Nantong Fellow-Provincials Association stating: 'According to a letter jointly signed by our association members Feng Daoyuan and more than 200 others, the "tada" cart industry relies on manpower to transport goods for customers, working hard to make a living. Since the development of mechanical transportation and the emergence of trucks that monopolize the market, business has been declining, and the huge seasonal taxes (10 yuan per season) must be paid reluctantly. The hardships are numerous, and we are worried about freezing and starvation. Now, several industries in Shanghai are declining, and the situation is unprecedentedly bleak. Our industry is on the verge of collapse due to the sharp decline in passenger and cargo traffic. Unexpectedly, news has come that the Public Concession Municipal Council, disregarding the difficult times, has decided to increase the taxes on the "tada" cart industry by 50%. Upon hearing this, we were horrified. While it may increase the authorities' income, the increased levies will directly declare the "tada" cart industry dead and indirectly increase social concerns. After discussion, we unanimously expressed our inability to bear the tax increase and specially requested your association to consider the plight of our fellow townsmen and the hardships of the laboring class and provide assistance.' The "tada" cart industry is affected by the economic downturn and faces difficult livelihoods, which is a visible fact. Increasing taxes now will only speed up its collapse and increase the number of unemployed. According to the previous letter, we hereby request your association to consider the difficult times and the hardships of the "tada" cart industry and promptly strive to get the Public Concession Municipal Council to cancel the tax increase in order to secure their business." Representatives of the "tada" cart industry also sent a letter to the association with the same request. The tax increase on the rickshaw industry has already been brought to your attention in a letter requesting you to consider the difficult times and promptly cancel the tax increase. The previous reasons are the same, and we request you to quickly adapt to the social and economic environment and cancel the tax increase in order to secure the legitimate livelihood of the industry and avoid increasing the number of unemployed in society. This is our sincere hope."

Letter

To the Editor, I am writing in response to the news item "Concubine Sues Widow and Son After Overseas Chinese Lin Yuting's Death" published in your newspaper on the 18th of this month. It said, "Lin Yuting's estate, worth hundreds of thousands, is entirely managed by his legal wife and son Lin Ruobo. Now, Lin Yuting's concubine, Lin Jiangsong, has hired a lawyer to request the partition of the estate, on the grounds that she has been abused by the legal wife and son since her husband's death, making it unbearable to live together." This is far from the truth. After my late father's death, the estate was only around 40,000 to 50,000 yuan, and nearly half of it has been spent on household expenses in recent years. As for the allegations of abuse, they are even more untrue. Lin Jiangsong voluntarily left home after my late father's death, and there was no abuse. This must be a misunderstanding by your reporter based on hearsay. I hope you will correct this to reflect the truth. Sincerely, Lin Ruobo, July 18.

Zheng Zhengqiu's Coffin Sealed Yesterday, Temporarily Placed in the Chaozhou Bayi Mountain Villa in Jiangwan

The former pioneer of our film industry, director Zheng Zhengqiu of the Star Film Company, passed away on the 16th of this month at 7:00 AM due to heart failure. When the news came, everyone lamented the loss of a talent in our country's film industry. Zheng's remains were cremated at the Shanghai Funeral Home on Xujiahui Road yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, and the coffin was carried out at 3:00 PM, temporarily placed in the Chaozhou Bayi Mountain Villa in Jiangwan. The following details the tributes, meals, and funeral arrangements:

Tributes from All Sides

Yesterday, among the groups that came to pay their respects, besides the Star Film Company and the Star Revival Comrades Association, there were also the Hua Gan Company, Central Cinema Company, Xin Guang Grand Theater, Guangdong Fellow Association, Chaozhou Fellow Association, Chaozhou Guild Hall, Chaozhou Heji Hospital, Ju Sheng He Sports Ground, Xia Yi General Society, Zhi Guang General Society, Ming De Charity Hall, Qun An Righteous School, Zheng clan members, and the film industry (including Lianhua, Diantong, Tianyi, Jinan, Wenhua, and other film companies), as well as dozens of new drama groups, totaling over a thousand people.

Sealing of the Coffin at 2:00 PM

Zheng's remains were sealed in a coffin at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon in the Shanghai Funeral Home's auditorium. Condolence banners and messages from all walks of life hung all around, and the coffin was covered with wreaths. An altar table was set up in front of the spirit, with a portrait hanging above it. The public memorial service began at around 3:00 PM. Pan Gongzhan, chairman of the Star Film Company's board of directors, presided over the ceremony, and Yan Gongshang read the eulogy. Afterwards, various groups successively paid their respects before the spirit, and the ceremony concluded around 3:00 PM.

Star Film Company's Eulogy

The eulogy from the Star Film Company's board of directors reads: On this eighteenth day of July, the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China, the Star Film Company's board of directors respectfully offers incense, flowers, and clear wine in tribute to the late Director and Associate Manager of our company, Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu, saying: Alas, how painful! With your outstanding talent, you founded the company and laid the foundation for the Chinese film industry. You were enthusiastic about public welfare and engaged in social causes for decades. Your great reputation was admired by the entire country. In recent years, the company's situation was difficult and dangerous. You again contributed your savings to the silver screen. Each film released was praised by everyone as a "Saint of Chinese Directors." Therefore, the company was able to survive amidst hardship, thanks to your great efforts. Our association deeply celebrates having you. Unexpectedly, the sad news came that you passed away suddenly on the sixteenth of this month. Alas, how sorrowful! Your loss is not only the great misfortune of our company, but also a great loss to the Chinese film industry. Alas, how painful! With grief and tears, there is no way to express our feelings. We respectfully hope...

Carrying the Coffin at 3:00 PM

The coffin was carried out at around 3:00 PM. More than a dozen people, including Zhang Youchuan, Zhou Jianyun, Hu Die, Shen Xiling, Li Pingqian, Cheng Bugao, Gao Jilin, Xuan Jinglin, and Wang Qianbai, participated in carrying the coffin and boarding the hearse. Family members and guests also boarded over a hundred cars specially prepared by Zheng's funeral committee to see him off.

Funeral Procession

The funeral procession was led by a large white banner with black borders reading "The Funeral of Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu." Following were the Municipal Police Bureau band, a vehicle carrying a portrait, the hearse, and then the cars of family members, guests, and mourners, totaling over a hundred vehicles. They turned from Xujiahui Road onto Avenue Albert, passing through Avenue Foch, Xizang Road, North Xizang Road, Haining Road, North Zhejiang Road, Boundary Road, Baoshan Road, Qixing Road, Liuying Road, and Xinshi Road, reaching the Chaozhou Bayi Villa in Jiangwan Town. The mourners paid their respects before the spirit before dispersing. The Star Film Company filmed the entire funeral. In addition, the funeral committee prepared a box of Guanshengyuan fruits and snacks for each guest.

Condolence Telegrams from Various Places

After the news of Zheng's death reached various places, many of his friends sent telegrams of condolence. The funeral committee received messages from Chen Bonan in Guangdong, Hong Shen in Qingdao, Fang Zhi in Nanjing, Zhang Chong, the Central Film Enterprise Committee, the Chinese Educational Film Association, colleagues from the Film Section of the Central Propaganda Department, the Hong Kong Huawi Company, and dozens of other groups and individuals.

Recent Bull Squeeze in Cotton Market Becomes Increasingly Apparent

The cotton market's upward trend is intensifying, with the July and August futures contracts showing particularly strong upward momentum. This is due to bullish traders controlling the market and remaining steadfast, deepening the expectation of a short squeeze. Many short sellers are showing signs of panic, and covering their positions is not uncommon. New cotton futures for distant months have also been spurred to rise. According to market sources, the severe flooding in the Hubei region has led to rumors that cotton production will only reach 20% of normal levels, resulting in a surge of new buyers.

A Glimpse of Short Covering Frenzy

At the opening of the Shanghai Cotton Exchange, the market situation for all months remained stable initially. Near-month contracts were weaker due to selling pressure from Changfeng, but distant-month contracts were tighter, rising by 1 to 2 jiao. Buying interest surged during the second and third trading sessions, with short sellers covering their positions in near-month contracts and bullish traders unwilling to release their holdings, causing the market to rise further and further. Regarding new cotton, rumors of severe flooding in Hankou, with only 20% of the crop secured, led to an even greater influx of buyers, pushing prices up rapidly. As a result, all months closed higher than the previous day, with gains ranging from 4.5 to 6.5 jiao. The reported sales were: Mei Ji 2,600 dan, Tong Ji 2,800 dan, Yuan Da 3,300 dan, Jun Chang 1,800 dan, Yi Chang 1,800 dan, Changfeng 3,900 dan, Jian Kang 1,700 dan, and Yuan Xing Chang 2,200 dan. Grains: Flour Lacks Upward Momentum

The flour market initially continued its positive trend but then leveled off. This was because Chicago prices rose by around 1 yuan for near-term contracts and 7-8 jiao for distant-term contracts. Canadian wheat rose by 1 jiao. Market sentiment initially favored foreign wheat, capitalizing on the previous day's momentum. Recent bids continued to be strong, rising by about 1 fen, but market sentiment remained stable during the second trading session. However, as large mills increased their selling, the market turned downwards from the third trading session onwards. Subsequent trading became sparse, with little activity on both sides. Domestically, all wheat-producing areas have been affected by flooding, making the future of grains a matter that cannot be taken lightly. However, due to tight credit, traders are inevitably hesitant, resulting in weaker buying power than before, which is also preventing the market from rebounding strongly. As a result, the current month remained unchanged, August rose slightly by 0.5 fen, September remained unchanged, October rose by 0.25 li, November rose by 0.5 fen, and December remained unchanged.

Medium-quality goods were mostly stable. As for Yinbian Yuan rice, its price had been falling daily, but now it has shown signs of rebounding by 3 jiao. The price of Du Jian rice is volatile.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, arrivals from various river ports were around 1,000 bags. Various grades of polished, white japonica rice continued to sell, and prices for high-quality goods were expected to rise. Prices for medium- and lower-quality goods edged up by nearly 1 jiao. Thin indica rice was scarce and rose by 1-2 jiao. Early rice was stable, and Zijinling rice was selling actively, rising by 3-4 jiao. The prices of other goods remained mostly unchanged.

Imported Rice: Medium and Lower Grades Edge Up Slightly

Yesterday, the imported rice market showed signs of weakening again. Although shipments were still being arranged along the Yangtze River, sales were minimal, unlike the domestic merchants who sold thousands of bags. Ningbo merchants were inquiring about medium- and lower-grade goods, but high-quality rice from Ningbo was experiencing slow sales and was being shipped to Shanghai for sale, which was the main reason for the market's weakness. Yesterday, sales of small and medium grades were weak, while there was no demand from hoarders for high-quality Saigon rice. Therefore, the prices of high-quality rice remained stable, while other grades edged up slightly. Total sales for the city amounted to more than 7,000 bags, with merchants from Hankou, Jiujiang, Nanjing, Ningbo, and the local market purchasing the goods. Domestic merchants have completely stopped buying.
